# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# LLVM Pass Manager Registration and Execution Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a new LLVM optimization pass is registered and executed in llvm/llvm-project. Find C++ source files that define: the PassManager template, the PassRegistry, the pass add() registration, and the pass execution order in the standard optimization pipeline (O2/O3).

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d, sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

Perfect! I've completed the analysis and created the answer.json file. Here's a summary of what I found:

## LLVM Pass Manager Registration and Execution Chain

I've traced how LLVM optimization passes are registered and executed by analyzing the key files in the llvm/llvm-project repository. The system involves several critical components:

### Key Components:

1. **PassManager Template** (`llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h`):
   - Manages sequences of passes over IR units (Modules, Functions, Loops)
   - Uses concept-based polymorphism for type-safe pass management
   - The `addPass()` method registers passes for execution

2. **PassRegistry** (`llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h` and `llvm/lib/IR/PassRegistry.cpp`):
   - Global singleton registry for pass information
   - Stores PassInfo objects indexed by type ID and string name
   - Used for pass lookup and dependency resolution

3. **PassBuilder** (`llvm/include/llvm/Passes/PassBuilder.h`):
   - Constructs standard optimization pipelines (O2/O3)
   - Key methods:
     - `buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline()` - top-level per-module pipeline
     - `buildModuleSimplificationPipeline()` - canonicalization passes
     - `buildModuleOptimizationPipeline()` - speed optimization passes

4. **Pipeline Implementation** (`llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilderPipelines.cpp`):
   - Implements the actual O2/O3 optimization pipeline
   - Includes passes like loop rotation, vectorization, inlining, dead code elimination
   - Uses hierarchical pass managers for different IR levels (Module → Function → Loop)

5. **Pass Registry Definitions** (`llvm/lib/Passes/PassRegistry.def`):
   - Macro-based definitions of all available passes
   - Allows passes to be named and constructed on demand

### Execution Flow:
When a module is optimized at O2/O3:

There\\n11: /// is no \\\"pass\\\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\\n12: /// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\\n13: /// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\\n14: /// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\\n15: /// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\\n16: /// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\\n17: /// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\\n18: /// single module provided.\\n19: ///\\n20: /// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\\n21: /// modules and functions.\\n22: ///\\n23: /// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\\n24: ///   a Function.\\n25: /// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\\n26: ///\\n27: /// Note that the implementations of the pass managers class Module;\\n62: \\n63: // Forward declare the analysis manager template.\\n64: template <typename IRUnitT, typename... ExtraArgTs> class AnalysisManager;\\n65: \\n66: /// A CRTP mix-in to automatically provide informational APIs needed for\\n67: /// passes.\\n68: ///\\n69: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are passes.\\n70: template <typename DerivedT> struct PassInfoMixin {\\n71:   /// Gets the name of the pass we are mixed into.\\n72:   static StringRef name() {\\n73:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<PassInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\\n74:                   \\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\");\\n75:     StringRef Name = getTypeName<DerivedT>();\\n76:     Name.consume_front(\\\"llvm::\\\");\\n77:     return Name;\\n78:   }\\n79: \\n80:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\\n81:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\\n82:     StringRef ClassName = DerivedT::name();\\n83:     auto PassName = MapClassName2PassName(ClassName);\\n84:     OS << PassName;\\n85:   }\\n86: };\\n87: \\n88: /// A CRTP mix-in that provides informational APIs needed for analysis passes.\\n89: ///\\n90: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are analysis passes. It\\n91: /// automatically mixes in \\\\c PassInfoMixin.\\n92: template <typename DerivedT>\\n93: struct AnalysisInfoMixin : PassInfoMixin<DerivedT> {\\n94:   /// Returns an opaque, unique ID for this analysis type.\\n95:   ///\\n96:   /// This ID is a pointer type that is guaranteed to be 8-byte aligned and thus\\n97:   /// suitable for use in sets, maps, and other data structures that use the low\\n98:   /// bits of pointers.\\n99:   ///\\n100:   /// Note that this requires the derived type provide a static \\\\c AnalysisKey\\n101:   /// member called \\\\c Key.\\n102:   ///\\n103:   /// FIXME: The only reason the mixin type itself can't declare the Key value\\n104:   /// is that some compilers cannot correctly unique a templated static variable\\n105:   /// so it has the same addresses in each instantiation. The only currently\\n106:   /// known platform with this limitation is Windows DLL builds, specifically\\n107:   /// building each part of LLVM as a DLL. If we ever remove that build\\n108:   /// configuration, this mixin can provide the static key as well.\\n109:   static AnalysisKey *ID() {\\n110:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<AnalysisInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\\n111:                   \\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\");\\n112:     return &DerivedT::Key;\\n113:   }\\n114: };\\n115: \\n116: namespace detail {\\n117: \\n118: /// Actual unpacker of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult,\\n119: /// passes only those tuple arguments that are mentioned in index_sequence.\\n120: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename AnalysisManagerT,\\n121:           typename... ArgTs, size_t... Ns>\\n122: typename PassT::Result\\n123: getAnalysisResultUnpackTuple(AnalysisManagerT &AM, IRUnitT &IR,\\n124:                              std::tuple<ArgTs...> Args,\\n125:                              std::index_sequence<Ns...>) {\\n126:   (void)Args;\\n127:   return AM.template getResult<PassT>(IR, std::get<Ns>(Args)...);\\n128: }\\n129: \\n130: /// Helper for *partial* unpacking of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult.\\n131: ///\\n132: /// Arguments passed in tuple come from PassManager, so they might have extra\\n133: /// arguments after those AnalysisManager's ExtraArgTs ones that we need to\\n134: /// pass to getResult.\\n135: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename... It is itself a valid pass over that unit of\\n151: /// IR, and when run over some given IR will run each of its contained passes in\\n152: /// sequence. Pass managers are the primary and most basic building block of a\\n153: /// pass pipeline.\\n154: ///\\n155: /// When you run a pass manager, you provide an \\\\c AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>\\n156: /// argument. The pass manager will propagate that analysis manager to each\\n157: /// pass it runs, and will call the analysis manager's invalidation routine with\\n158: /// the PreservedAnalyses of each pass it runs.\\n159: template <typename IRUnitT,\\n160:           typename AnalysisManagerT = AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>,\\n161:           typename... ExtraArgTs>\\n162: class PassManager : public PassInfoMixin<\\n163:                         PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>> {\\n164: public:\\n165:   /// Construct a pass manager.\\n166:   explicit PassManager() = default;\\n167: \\n168:   // FIXME: These are equivalent to the default move constructor/move\\n169:   // assignment. However, using = default triggers linker errors due to the\\n170:   // explicit instantiations below. Find away to use the default and remove the\\n171:   // duplicated code here.\\n172:   PassManager(PassManager &&Arg) : Passes(std::move(Arg.Passes)) {}\\n173: \\n174:   PassManager &operator=(PassManager &&RHS) {\\n175:     Passes = std::move(RHS.Passes);\\n176:     return *this;\\n177:   }\\n178: \\n179:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\\n180:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\\n181:     ListSeparator LS(\\\",\\\");\\n182:     for (auto &P : Passes) {\\n183:       OS << LS;\\n184:       P->printPipeline(OS, MapClassName2PassName);\\n185:     }\\n186:   }\\n187: \\n188:   /// Run all of the passes in this manager over the given unit of IR.\\n189:   /// ExtraArgs are passed to each pass.\\n190:   PreservedAnalyses run(IRUnitT &IR, AnalysisManagerT &AM,\\n191:                         ExtraArgTs... ExtraArgs);\\n192: \\n193:   template <typename PassT>\\n194:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<!std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n195:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n196:     using PassModelT =\\n197:         detail::PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n198:     // Do not use make_unique or emplace_back, they cause too many template\\n199:     // instantiations, causing terrible compile times.\\n200:     Passes.push_back(std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>(\\n201:         new PassModelT(std::forward<PassT>(Pass))));\\n202:   }\\n203: \\n204:   /// When adding a pass manager pass that has the same type as this pass\\n205:   /// manager, simply move the passes over. This is because we don't have\\n206:   /// use cases rely on executing nested pass managers. Doing this could\\n207:   /// reduce implementation complexity and avoid potential invalidation\\n208:   /// issues that may happen with nested pass managers of the same type.\\n209:   template <typename PassT>\\n210:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n211:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n212:     for (auto &P : Pass.Passes)\\n213:       Passes.push_back(std::move(P));\\n214:   }\\n215: \\n216:   /// Returns if the pass manager contains any passes.\\n217:   bool isEmpty() const { return Passes.empty(); }\\n218: \\n219:   static bool isRequired() { return true; }\\n220: \\n221: protected:\\n222:   using PassConceptT =\\n223:       detail::PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n224: \\n225:   std::vector<std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> Passes;\\n226: };\\n227: \\n228: template <typename IRUnitT>\\n229: void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace(raw_ostream &OS, const IRUnitT &IR);\\n230: \\n231: template <>\\n232: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Module>(raw_ostream &OS,\\n233:                                                    const Module &IR);\\n234: \\n235: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Module>;\\n236: \\n237: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over modules.\\n238: using ModulePassManager = PassManager<Module>;\\n239: \\n240: template <>\\n241: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Function>(raw_ostream &OS,\\n242:                                                      const Function &IR);\\n243: \\n244: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Function>;\\n245: \\n246: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over functions.\\n247: using FunctionPassManager = PassManager<Function>;\\n248: \\n249: /// A container for analyses that lazily runs them and caches their\\n250: /// results.\\n251: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d@4152de6435984e9fc55431f4d74a7470d8ac05c0/-/blob/llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h%3FL1-250\"}",

If we ever remove that build\n108:   /// configuration, this mixin can provide the static key as well.\n109:   static AnalysisKey *ID() {\n110:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<AnalysisInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\n111:                   \"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\");\n112:     return &DerivedT::Key;\n113:   }\n114: };\n115: \n116: namespace detail {\n117: \n118: /// Actual unpacker of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult,\n119: /// passes only those tuple arguments that are mentioned in index_sequence.\n120: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename AnalysisManagerT,\n121:           typename... ArgTs, size_t... Ns>\n122: typename PassT::Result\n123: getAnalysisResultUnpackTuple(AnalysisManagerT &AM, IRUnitT &IR,\n124:                              std::tuple<ArgTs...> Args,\n125:                              std::index_sequence<Ns...>) {\n126:   (void)Args;\n127:   return AM.template getResult<PassT>(IR, std::get<Ns>(Args)...);\n128: }\n129: \n130: /// Helper for *partial* unpacking of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult.\n131: ///\n132: /// Arguments passed in tuple come from PassManager, so they might have extra\n133: /// arguments after those AnalysisManager's ExtraArgTs ones that we need to\n134: /// pass to getResult.\n135: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename... AnalysisArgTs,\n136:           typename... MainArgTs>\n137: typename PassT::Result\n138: getAnalysisResult(AnalysisManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisArgTs...> &AM, IRUnitT &IR,\n139:                   std::tuple<MainArgTs...> Args) {\n140:   return (getAnalysisResultUnpackTuple<\n141:           PassT, IRUnitT>)(AM, IR, Args,\n142:                            std::index_sequence_for<AnalysisArgTs...>{});\n143: }\n144: \n145: } // namespace detail\n146: \n147: /// Manages a sequence of passes over a particular unit of IR.\n148: ///\n149: /// A pass manager contains a sequence of passes to run over a particular unit\n150: /// of IR (e.g. Functions, Modules). It is itself a valid pass over that unit of\n151: /// IR, and when run over some given IR will run each of its contained passes in\n152: /// sequence. Pass managers are the primary and most basic building block of a\n153: /// pass pipeline.\n154: ///\n155: /// When you run a pass manager, you provide an \\c AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>\n156: /// argument. The pass manager will propagate that analysis manager to each\n157: /// pass it runs, and will call the analysis manager's invalidation routine with\n158: /// the PreservedAnalyses of each pass it runs.\n159: template <typename IRUnitT,\n160:           typename AnalysisManagerT = AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>,\n161:           typename... ExtraArgTs>\n162: class PassManager : public PassInfoMixin<\n163:                         PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>> {\n164: public:\n165:   /// Construct a pass manager.\n166:   explicit PassManager() = default;\n167: \n168:   // FIXME: These are equivalent to the default move constructor/move\n169:   // assignment. However, using = default triggers linker errors due to the\n170:   // explicit instantiations below. Find away to use the default and remove the\n171:   // duplicated code here.\n172:   PassManager(PassManager &&Arg) : Passes(std::move(Arg.Passes)) {}\n173: \n174:   PassManager &operator=(PassManager &&RHS) {\n175:     Passes = std::move(RHS.Passes);\n176:     return *this;\n177:   }\n178: \n179:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\n180:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\n181:     ListSeparator LS(\",\");\n182:     for (auto &P : Passes) {\n183:       OS << LS;\n184:       P->printPipeline(OS, MapClassName2PassName);\n185:     }\n186:   }\n187: \n188:   /// Run all of the passes in this manager over the given unit of IR.\n189:   /// ExtraArgs are passed to each pass.\n190:   PreservedAnalyses run(IRUnitT &IR, AnalysisManagerT &AM,\n191:                         ExtraArgTs... ExtraArgs);\n192: \n193:   template <typename PassT>\n194:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<!std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\n195:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\n196:     using PassModelT =\n197:         detail::PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\n198:     // Do not use make_unique or emplace_back, they cause too many template\n199:     // instantiations, causing terrible compile times.\n200:     Passes.push_back(std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>(\n201:         new PassModelT(std::forward<PassT>(Pass))));\n202:   }\n203: \n204:   /// When adding a pass manager pass that has the same type as this pass\n205:   /// manager, simply move the passes over. This is because we don't have\n206:   /// use cases rely on executing nested pass managers. Doing this could\n207:   /// reduce implementation complexity and avoid potential invalidation\n208:   /// issues that may happen with nested pass managers of the same type.\n209:   template <typename PassT>\n210:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\n211:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\n212:     for (auto &P : Pass.Passes)\n213:       Passes.push_back(std::move(P));\n214:   }\n215: \n216:   /// Returns if the pass manager contains any passes.\n217:   bool isEmpty() const { return Passes.empty(); }\n218: \n219:   static bool isRequired() { return true; }\n220: \n221: protected:\n222:   using PassConceptT =\n223:       detail::PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\n224: \n225:   std::vector<std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> Passes;\n226: };\n227: \n228: template <typename IRUnitT>\n229: void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace(raw_ostream &OS, const IRUnitT &IR);\n230: \n231: template <>\n232: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Module>(raw_ostream &OS,\n233:                                                    const Module &IR);\n234: \n235: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Module>;\n236: \n237: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over modules.\n238: using ModulePassManager = PassManager<Module>;\n239: \n240: template <>\n241: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Function>(raw_ostream &OS,\n242:                                                      const Function &IR);\n243: \n244: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Function>;\n245: \n246: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over functions.\n247: using FunctionPassManager = PassManager<Function>;\n248: \n249: /// A container for analyses that lazily runs them and caches their\n250: /// results.\n251: ",

Its default value\\n69:   /// is that of the flag: `-forget-scev-loop-unroll`.\\n70:   bool ForgetAllSCEVInLoopUnroll;\\n71: \\n72:   /// Tuning option to cap the number of calls to retrive clobbering accesses in\\n73:   /// MemorySSA, in LICM.\\n74:   unsigned LicmMssaOptCap;\\n75: \\n76:   /// Tuning option to disable promotion to scalars in LICM with MemorySSA, if\\n77:   /// the number of access is too large.\\n78:   unsigned LicmMssaNoAccForPromotionCap;\\n79: \\n80:   /// Tuning option to enable/disable call graph profile. Its default value is\\n81:   /// that of the flag: `-enable-npm-call-graph-profile`.\\n82:   bool CallGraphProfile;\\n83: \\n84:   // Add LTO pipeline tuning option to enable the unified LTO pipeline.\\n85:   bool UnifiedLTO;\\n86: \\n87:   /// Tuning option to enable/disable function merging. Its default value is\\n88:   /// false.\\n89:   bool MergeFunctions;\\n90: \\n91:   /// Tuning option to override the default inliner threshold.\\n92:   int InlinerThreshold;\\n93: \\n94:   // Experimental option to eagerly invalidate more analyses. This has the\\n95:   // potential to decrease max memory usage in exchange for more compile time.\\n96:   // This may affect codegen due to either passes using analyses only when\\n97:   // cached, or invalidating and recalculating an analysis that was\\n98:   // stale/imprecise but still valid. Currently this invalidates all function\\n99:   // analyses after various module->function or cgscc->function adaptors in the\\n100:   // default pipelines.\\n101:   bool EagerlyInvalidateAnalyses;\\n102: \\n103:   // Tuning option to enable/disable speculative devirtualization.\\n104:   // Its default value is false.\\n105:   bool DevirtualizeSpeculatively;\\n106: };\\n107: \\n108: /// This class provides access to building LLVM's passes.\\n109: ///\\n110: /// Its members provide the baseline state available to passes during their\\n111: /// construction. The \\\\c PassRegistry.def file specifies how to construct all\\n112: /// of the built-in passes, and those may reference these members during\\n113: /// construction.\\n114: class PassBuilder {\\n115:   TargetMachine *TM;\\n116:   PipelineTuningOptions PTO;\\n117:   std::optional<PGOOptions> PGOOpt;\\n118:   PassInstrumentationCallbacks *PIC;\\n119:   IntrusiveRefCntPtr<vfs::FileSystem> FS;\\n120: \\n121: public:\\n122:   /// A struct to capture parsed pass pipeline names.\\n123:   ///\\n124:   /// A pipeline is defined as a series of names, each of which may in itself\\n125:   /// recursively contain a nested pipeline. A name is either the name of a pass\\n126:   /// (e.g. \\\"instcombine\\\") or the name of a pipeline type (e.g. \\\"cgscc\\\"). If the\\n127:   /// name is the name of a pass, the InnerPipeline is empty, since passes\\n128:   /// cannot contain inner pipelines. See parsePassPipeline() for a more\\n129:   /// detailed description of the textual pipeline format.\\n130:   struct PipelineElement {\\n131:     StringRef Name;\\n132:     std::vector<PipelineElement> InnerPipeline;\\n133:   };\\n134: \\n135:   LLVM_ABI explicit PassBuilder(\\n136:       TargetMachine *TM = nullptr,\\n137:       PipelineTuningOptions PTO = PipelineTuningOptions(),\\n138:       std::optional<PGOOptions> PGOOpt = std::nullopt,\\n139:       PassInstrumentationCallbacks *PIC = nullptr,\\n140:       IntrusiveRefCntPtr<vfs::FileSystem> FS = vfs::getRealFileSystem());\\n141: \\n142:   /// Cross register the analysis managers through their proxies.\\n143:   ///\\n144:   /// This is an interface that can be used to cross register each\\n145:   /// AnalysisManager with all the others analysis managers.\\n146:   LLVM_ABI void\\n147:   crossRegisterProxies(LoopAnalysisManager &LAM, FunctionAnalysisManager &FAM,\\n148:                        CGSCCAnalysisManager &CGAM, ModuleAnalysisManager &MAM,\\n149:                        MachineFunctionAnalysisManager *MFAM = nullptr);\\n150: \\n151:   /// Registers all available module analysis passes.\\n152:   ///\\n153:   /// This is an interface that can be used to populate a \\\\c\\n154:   /// ModuleAnalysisManager with all registered module analyses. Callers can\\n155:   /// still manually register any additional analyses. Callers can also\\n156:   /// pre-register analyses and this will not override those.\\n157:   LLVM_ABI void registerModuleAnalyses(ModuleAnalysisManager &MAM);\\n158: \\n159:   /// Registers all available CGSCC analysis passes.\\n160:   ///\\n161:   /// This is an interface that can be used to populate a \\\\c CGSCCAnalysisManager\\n162:   /// with all registered CGSCC analyses. Callers can still manually register any\\n163:   /// additional analyses. Callers can also pre-register analyses and this will\\n164:   /// not override those.\\n165:   LLVM_ABI void registerCGSCCAnalyses(CGSCCAnalysisManager &CGAM);\\n166: \\n167:   /// Registers all available function analysis passes.\\n168:   ///\\n169:   /// This is an interface that can be used to populate a \\\\c\\n170:   /// FunctionAnalysisManager with all registered function analyses. Callers can\\n171:   /// still manually register any additional analyses. Callers can also\\n172:   /// pre-register analyses and this will not override those.\\n173:   LLVM_ABI void registerFunctionAnalyses(FunctionAnalysisManager &FAM);\\n174: \\n175:   /// Registers all available loop analysis passes.\\n176:   ///\\n177:   /// This is an interface that can be used to populate a \\\\c LoopAnalysisManager\\n178:   /// with all registered loop analyses. Callers can still manually register any\\n179:   /// additional analyses.\\n180:   LLVM_ABI void registerLoopAnalyses(LoopAnalysisManager &LAM);\\n181: \\n182:   /// Registers all available machine function analysis passes.\\n183:   ///\\n184:   /// This is an interface that can be used to populate a \\\\c\\n185:   /// MachineFunctionAnalysisManager with all registered function analyses.\\n186:   /// Callers can still manually register any additional analyses. Callers can\\n187:   /// also pre-register analyses and this will not override those.\\n188:   LLVM_ABI void\\n189:   registerMachineFunctionAnalyses(MachineFunctionAnalysisManager &MFAM);\\n190: \\n191:   /// Construct the core LLVM function canonicalization and simplification\\n192:   /// pipeline.\\n193:   ///\\n194:   /// This is a long pipeline and uses most of the per-function optimization\\n195:   /// passes in LLVM to canonicalize and simplify the IR. It is suitable to run\\n196:   /// repeatedly over the IR and is not expected to destroy important\\n197:   /// information about the semantics of the IR.\\n198:   ///\\n199:   /// Note that \\\\p Level cannot be `O0` here. The pipelines produced are\\n200:   /// only intended for use when attempting to optimize code. If frontends\\n201:   /// require some transformations for semantic reasons, they should explicitly\\n202:   /// build them.\\n203:   ///\\n204:   /// \\\\p Phase indicates the current ThinLTO phase.\\n205:   LLVM_ABI FunctionPassManager buildFunctionSimplificationPipeline(\\n206:       OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\\n207: \\n208:   /// Construct the core LLVM module canonicalization and simplification\\n209:   /// pipeline.\\n210:   ///\\n211:   /// This pipeline focuses on canonicalizing and simplifying the entire module\\n212:   /// of IR. Much like the function simplification pipeline above, it is\\n213:   /// suitable to run repeatedly over the IR and is not expected to destroy\\n214:   /// important information. It does, however, perform inlining and other\\n215:   /// heuristic based simplifications that are not strictly reversible.\\n216:   ///\\n217:   /// Note that \\\\p Level cannot be `O0` here. The pipelines produced are\\n218:   /// only intended for use when attempting to optimize code. If frontends\\n219:   /// require some transformations for semantic reasons, they should explicitly\\n220:   /// build them.\\n221:   ///\\n222:   /// \\\\p Phase indicates the current ThinLTO phase.\\n223:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildModuleSimplificationPipeline(\\n224:       OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\\n225: \\n226:   /// Construct the module pipeline that performs inlining as well as\\n227:   /// the inlining-driven cleanups.\\n228:   LLVM_ABI ModuleInlinerWrapperPass\\n229:   buildInlinerPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\\n230: \\n231:   /// Construct the module pipeline that performs inlining with\\n232:   /// module inliner pass.\\n233:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\\n234:   buildModuleInlinerPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\\n235: \\n236:   /// Construct the core LLVM module optimization pipeline.\\n237:   ///\\n238:   /// This pipeline focuses on optimizing the execution speed of the IR. It\\n239:   /// uses cost modeling and thresholds to balance code growth against runtime\\n240:   /// improvements. It includes vectorization and other information destroying\\n241:   /// transformations. It also cannot generally be run repeatedly on a module\\n242:   /// without potentially seriously regressing either runtime performance of\\n243:   /// the code or serious code size growth.\\n244:   ///\\n245:   /// Note that \\\\p Level cannot be `O0` here. The pipelines produced are\\n246:   /// only intended for use when attempting to optimize code. If frontends\\n247:   /// require some transformations for semantic reasons, they should explicitly\\n248:   /// build them.\\n249:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildModuleOptimizationPipeline(\\n250:       OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase LTOPhase);\\n251: \\n252:   /// Build a per-module default optimization pipeline.\\n253:   ///\\n254:   /// This provides a good default optimization pipeline for per-module\\n255:   /// optimization and code generation without any link-time optimization. It\\n256:   /// typically correspond to frontend \\\"-O[123]\\\" options for optimization\\n257:   /// levels \\\\c O1, \\\\c O2 and \\\\c O3 resp.\\n258:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline(\\n259:       OptimizationLevel Level,\\n260:       ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase = ThinOrFullLTOPhase::None);\\n261: \\n262:   /// Build a fat object default optimization pipeline.\\n263:   ///\\n264:   /// This builds a pipeline that runs the LTO/ThinLTO  pre-link pipeline, and\\n265:   /// emits a section containing the pre-link bitcode along side the object code\\n266:   /// generated in non-LTO compilation.\\n267:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildFatLTODefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level,\\n268:                                                         bool ThinLTO,\\n269:                                                         bool EmitSummary);\\n270: \\n271:   /// Build a pre-link, ThinLTO-targeting default optimization pipeline to\\n272:   /// a pass manager.\\n273:   ///\\n274:   /// This adds the pre-link optimizations tuned to prepare a module for\\n275:   /// a ThinLTO run. It works to minimize the IR which needs to be analyzed\\n276:   /// without making irreversible decisions which could be made better during\\n277:   /// the LTO run.\\n278:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\\n279:   buildThinLTOPreLinkDefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level);\\n280: \\n281:   /// Build a ThinLTO default optimization pipeline to a pass manager.\\n282:   ///\\n283:   /// This provides a good default optimization pipeline for link-time\\n284:   /// optimization and code generation. It is particularly tuned to fit well\\n285:   /// when IR coming into the LTO phase was first run through \\\\c\\n286:   /// buildThinLTOPreLinkDefaultPipeline, and the two coordinate closely.\\n287:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildThinLTODefaultPipeline(\\n288:       OptimizationLevel Level, const ModuleSummaryIndex *ImportSummary);\\n289: \\n290:   /// Build a pre-link, LTO-targeting default optimization pipeline to a pass\\n291:   /// manager.\\n292:   ///\\n293:   /// This adds the pre-link optimizations tuned to work well with a later LTO\\n294:   /// run. It works to minimize the IR which needs to be analyzed without\\n295:   /// making irreversible decisions which could be made better during the LTO\\n296:   /// run.\\n297:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\\n298:   buildLTOPreLinkDefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level);\\n299: \\n300:   /// Build an LTO default optimization pipeline to a pass manager.\\n301:   ///\\n302:   /// This provides a good default optimization pipeline for link-time\\n303:   /// optimization and code generation. It is particularly tuned to fit well\\n304:   /// when IR coming into the LTO phase was first run through \\\\c\\n305:   /// buildLTOPreLinkDefaultPipeline, and the two coordinate closely.\\n306:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildLTODefaultPipeline(\\n307:       OptimizationLevel Level, ModuleSummaryIndex *ExportSummary);\\n308: \\n309:   /// Build an O0 pipeline with the minimal semantically required passes.\\n310:   ///\\n311:   /// This should only be used for non-LTO and LTO pre-link pipelines.\\n312:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\\n313:   buildO0DefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level,\\n314:                          ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase = ThinOrFullLTOPhase::None);\\n315: \\n316:   /// Build the default `AAManager` with the default alias analysis pipeline\\n317:   /// registered.\\n318:   ///\\n319:   /// This also adds target-specific alias analyses registered via\\n320:   /// TargetMachine::registerDefaultAliasAnalyses().\\n321:   LLVM_ABI AAManager buildDefaultAAPipeline();\\n322: \\n323:   /// Parse a textual pass pipeline description into a \\\\c\\n324:   /// ModulePassManager.\\n325:   ///\\n326:   /// The format of the textual pass pipeline description looks something like:\\n327:   ///\\n328:   ///   module(function(instcombine,sroa),dce,cgscc(inliner,function(...)),...)\\n329:   ///\\n330:   /// Pass managers have ()s describing the nest structure of passes. All passes\\n331:   /// are comma separated. As a special shortcut, if the very first pass is not\\n332:   /// a module pass (as a module pass manager is), this will automatically form\\n333:   /// the shortest stack of pass managers that allow inserting that first pass.\\n334:   /// So, assuming function passes 'fpassN', CGSCC passes 'cgpassN', and loop\\n335:   /// passes 'lpassN', all of these are valid:\\n336:   ///\\n337:   ///   fpass1,fpass2,fpass3\\n338:   ///   cgpass1,cgpass2,cgpass3\\n339:   ///   lpass1,lpass2,lpass3\\n340:   ///\\n341:   /// And they are equivalent to the following (resp.):\\n342:   ///\\n343:   ///   module(function(fpass1,fpass2,fpass3))\\n344:   ///   module(cgscc(cgpass1,cgpass2,cgpass3))\\n345:   ///   module(function(loop(lpass1,lpass2,lpass3)))\\n346:   ///\\n347:   /// This shortcut is especially useful for debugging and testing small pass\\n348:   /// combinations.\\n349:   ///\\n350:   /// The sequence of passes aren't necessarily the exact same kind of pass.\\n351: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d@4152de6435984e9fc55431f4d74a7470d8ac05c0/-/blob/llvm/include/llvm/Passes/PassBuilder.h%3FL1-350\"}",

Much like the function simplification pipeline above, it is\n213:   /// suitable to run repeatedly over the IR and is not expected to destroy\n214:   /// important information. It does, however, perform inlining and other\n215:   /// heuristic based simplifications that are not strictly reversible.\n216:   ///\n217:   /// Note that \\p Level cannot be `O0` here. The pipelines produced are\n218:   /// only intended for use when attempting to optimize code. If frontends\n219:   /// require some transformations for semantic reasons, they should explicitly\n220:   /// build them.\n221:   ///\n222:   /// \\p Phase indicates the current ThinLTO phase.\n223:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildModuleSimplificationPipeline(\n224:       OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\n225: \n226:   /// Construct the module pipeline that performs inlining as well as\n227:   /// the inlining-driven cleanups.\n228:   LLVM_ABI ModuleInlinerWrapperPass\n229:   buildInlinerPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\n230: \n231:   /// Construct the module pipeline that performs inlining with\n232:   /// module inliner pass.\n233:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\n234:   buildModuleInlinerPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\n235: \n236:   /// Construct the core LLVM module optimization pipeline.\n237:   ///\n238:   /// This pipeline focuses on optimizing the execution speed of the IR. Other optimizations which runs later might get benefit of no-alias\n1544:   // assumption in clone loop.\n1545:   if (UseLoopVersioningLICM) {\n1546:     OptimizePM.addPass(\n1547:         createFunctionToLoopPassAdaptor(LoopVersioningLICMPass()));\n1548:     // LoopVersioningLICM pass might increase new LICM opportunities.\n1549:     OptimizePM.addPass(createFunctionToLoopPassAdaptor(\n1550:         LICMPass(PTO.LicmMssaOptCap, PTO.LicmMssaNoAccForPromotionCap,\n1551:                  /*AllowSpeculation=*/true),\n1552:         /*USeMemorySSA=*/true));\n1553:   }\n1554: \n1555:   OptimizePM.addPass(Float2IntPass());\n1556:   OptimizePM.addPass(LowerConstantIntrinsicsPass());\n1557: \n1558:   if (EnableMatrix) {\n1559:     OptimizePM.addPass(LowerMatrixIntrinsicsPass());\n1560:     OptimizePM.addPass(EarlyCSEPass());\n1561:   }\n1562: \n1563:   // CHR pass should only be applied with the profile information.\n1564:   // The check is to check the profile summary information in CHR.\n1565:   if (EnableCHR && Level == OptimizationLevel::O3)\n1566:     OptimizePM.addPass(ControlHeightReductionPass());\n1567: \n1568:   // FIXME: We need to run some loop optimizations to re-rotate loops after\n1569:   // simplifycfg and others undo their rotation.\n1570: \n1571:   // Optimize the loop execution. These passes operate on entire loop nests\n1572:   // rather than on each loop in an inside-out manner, and so they are actually\n1573:   // function passes.\n1574: \n1575:   invokeVectorizerStartEPCallbacks(OptimizePM, Level);\n1576: \n1577:   LoopPassManager LPM;\n1578:   // First rotate loops that may have been un-rotated by prior passes.\n1579:   // Disable header duplication at -Oz.\n1580:   LPM.addPass(LoopRotatePass(EnableLoopHeaderDuplication ||\n1581:                                  Level != OptimizationLevel::Oz,\n1582:                              LTOPreLink));\n1583:   // Some loops may have become dead by now. When preserved, this proxy will only invalidate results\\n46:   // cached on functions *still in the module* at the end of the module pass.\\n47:   auto PAC = PA.getChecker<FunctionAnalysisManagerModuleProxy>();\\n48:   if (!PAC.preserved() && !PAC.preservedSet<AllAnalysesOn<Module>>()) {\\n49:     InnerAM->clear();\\n50:     return true;\\n51:   }\\n52: \\n53:   // Directly check if the relevant set is preserved.\\n54:   bool AreFunctionAnalysesPreserved =\\n55:       PA.allAnalysesInSetPreserved<AllAnalysesOn<Function>>();\\n56: \\n57:   // Now walk all the functions to see if any inner analysis invalidation is\\n58:   // necessary.\\n59:   for (Function &F : M) {\\n60:     std::optional<PreservedAnalyses> FunctionPA;\\n61: \\n62:     // Check to proxy for this function.\\n65:     if (auto *OuterProxy =\\n66:             InnerAM->getCachedResult<ModuleAnalysisManagerFunctionProxy>(F))\\n67:       for (const auto &OuterInvalidationPair :\\n68: Analysis results are cached and invalidated based on pass requirements.\\n\\n3. **Extension Points**: PassBuilder provides callbacks for inserting custom passes:\\n   - registerOptimizerEarlyEPCallback() - early optimizer extension\\n   - registerOptimizerLastEPCallback() - late optimizer extension\\n   - registerPeepholeEPCallback() - peephole extension\\n   - registerVectorizerStartEPCallback(), registerVectorizerEndEPCallback()\\n\\n4. **Adaptor Pattern**: Uses ModuleToFunctionPassAdaptor and similar to run lower-level passes within higher-level pass managers\\n\\n5. **Hierarchical Execution**: Modules \u2192 Functions \u2192 Loops \u2192 Instructions with appropriate analysis managers at each level\"\n}\n",

Chain\\n\\n### Overview\\nLLVM uses a sophisticated pass infrastructure with two systems: the Legacy PassManager and the New PassManager. The New PassManager uses modern C++ template-based design with concept-based polymorphism.\\n\\n### PassManager Template (llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h)\\nThe core PassManager is a template class that manages sequences of passes over IR units (Modules, Functions, Loops, etc.). Key features:\\n- Template parameters: IRUnitT (e.g., Module, Function), AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs\\n- Specializations for ModulePassManager and FunctionPassManager (lines 238, 247)\\n- Uses `addPass()` template method (lines 193-214) which uses concept-based polymorphism\\n- Each pass is wrapped in a PassModel that implements the PassConcept interface\\n- Executes passes via the `run()` method which:\\n  1. Iterates through stored passes\\n  2. Calls each pass's run() method with the IR unit\\n  3. Updates analysis results based on PreservedAnalyses returned by each pass\\n\\n### PassRegistry (llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h and llvm/lib/IR/PassRegistry.cpp)\\nProvides global registration and lookup for passes:\\n- PassRegistry::getPassRegistry() returns the singleton global registry (PassRegistry.cpp:23-26)\\n- Stores PassInfo objects in two maps: by type ID and by string name (PassRegistry.h:42-46)\\n- registerPass() method adds PassInfo to both maps (PassRegistry.cpp:48-62)\\n- Used by legacy PassManager for dependency resolution\\n- Thread-unsafe by design - each thread needs its own registry\\n\\n### PassInfo (llvm/include/llvm/PassInfo.h)\\nMetadata class for passes containing:\\n- Pass name and command-line argument (lines 34-35)\\n- Pass ID pointer (type identifier) (line 36)\\n- Function pointer to pass constructor (line 39)\\n- Flags indicating analysis/CFG-only status (lines 37-38)\\n- Used primarily by legacy passes but referenced in modern infrastructure\\n\\n### PassBuilder (llvm/include/llvm/Passes/PassBuilder.h)\\nThe main class for constructing standard optimization pipelines:\\n- Holds TargetMachine, PipelineTuningOptions, PGOOptions\\n- Core pipeline building methods:\\n  - buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline() - per-module default pipeline for O1/O2/O3 (line 258)\\n  - buildModuleSimplificationPipeline() - canonicalization and simplification passes (line 223)\\n  - buildModuleOptimizationPipeline() - speed optimization passes (line 249)\\n  - buildInlinerPipeline() - inlining passes (line 228)\\n  - buildFunctionSimplificationPipeline() - per-function simplification (line 205)\\n\\n### Standard Optimization Pipeline (llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilderPipelines.cpp)\\nImplements the actual pipeline construction for O2/O3 optimization levels:\\n\\n**buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline (lines 1715-1761)**:\\n1. Returns O0 pipeline for O0 level\\n2. Adds memory profiling cleanup if non-LTO\\n3. Adds annotation to metadata conversion\\n4. Adds force function attributes\\n5. Calls buildModuleSimplificationPipeline (line 1746)\\n6. Calls buildModuleOptimizationPipeline (line 1749)\\n7. Adds LTO pre-link passes if applicable\\n\\n**buildModuleOptimizationPipeline (lines 1477-1651)**:\\nThis is the O2/O3 optimization pipeline that includes:\\n1. Partial inlining (line 1486)\\n2. For each registered pass (line 225 - Passes vector)\\n2. Retrieves PreservedAnalyses from previous pass\\n3. Calls pass's run() method with IR unit and AnalysisManager\\n4. AnalysisManager invalidates analyses based on PreservedAnalyses (lines 31-94 show invalidation logic)\\n5. ModuleToFunctionPassAdaptor (lines 107-148) adapts module passes to run on functions:\\n   - Gets FunctionAnalysisManager from module analysis manager\\n   - Runs function pass on each function\\n   - Handles analysis invalidation per-function\\n\\n### Key Design Patterns\\n\\n1. **Concept-Based Polymorphism**: PassManager uses type erasure through PassConcept and PassModel to support any pass type without virtual inheritance\\n\\n2. **Analysis Management**: Passes declare required/preserved analyses via PreservedAnalyses. Analysis results are cached and invalidated based on pass requirements.\\n\\n3. **Extension Points**: PassBuilder provides callbacks for inserting custom passes:\\n   - registerOptimizerEarlyEPCallback() - early optimizer extension\\n   - registerOptimizerLastEPCallback() - late optimizer extension\\n   - registerPeepholeEPCallback() - peephole extension\\n   - registerVectorizerStartEPCallback(), registerVectorizerEndEPCallback()\\n\\n4. **Adaptor Pattern**: Uses ModuleToFunctionPassAdaptor and similar to run lower-level passes within higher-level pass managers\\n\\n5. **Hierarchical Execution**: Modules \u2192 Functions \u2192 Loops \u2192 Instructions with appropriate analysis managers at each level\"\n}\n",
